Universe screen — 311 QC-confirmed ETFs raced vs. buy-and-hold

This week's big result: every screened ETF's best method panel is raced against always-long buy-and-hold; a deep-sweep then tries all axes × all labelers on the fit-relevant classes. The board ranks fits by edge over buy-and-hold, color-coded by trust tier.

Selection-bias warning. Each ETF is the best of a 49-config-per-ETF (21 axes + 27 labelers) best-of-N search — that search inflates the top result. TRUSTWORTHY fits (SSO, IAU, AGQ, DJP, GSG, UCO) are leak-re-verified with val_auc 0.57–0.66. PROVISIONAL fits (val_auc > 0.85: USO 0.98, GDX 0.96) are overfit / selection suspects — they need DSR deflation + a permuted-label control before deployment. Cash-ARTIFACT (Calmar inflated by ~0 MaxDD) and NO-BASELINE (degenerate 0-trade buy-hold, e.g. leveraged ETFs) are shown as excluded, not fits. ⓛ marks logdollar-axis fits (leak-re-verified).

What this is

An autonomous research loop that invents and back-tests single-ticker ETF trading strategies on real market data (QuantConnect), and keeps only the ones that beat buy-and-hold and survive strict out-of-sample + multiple-testing checks. The AI proposes and runs the experiments; a human steers.

Bottom line today — fully-validated single-ticker alpha is scarce: only GLD (gold trend-following, Calmar 4.02) and UUP (US-dollar regime, 1.30) clear every gate including the deflation (multiple-testing) check. But the loop is now screening all 311 QC-confirmed ETFs against buy-and-hold, and a cluster of commodity & leveraged-equity fits (IAU, GDX, USO, SSO, AGQ…) has surfaced — screen-strong and being validated before they earn a book seat. Each round attacks one ticker with two competing hypotheses and keeps a winner only if it clears every honest gate. The backtest is verified leak-free and fully online, using only models trained in the cloud (see deploy).

How to read the numbers
  • Calmar = annual return ÷ worst drawdown (higher is better; above 3 is strong).
  • MaxDD (MDD) = the deepest peak-to-trough loss along the way.
  • CAGR = compounded annual return. Sharpe = return per unit of volatility.
  • Edge = how much a strategy beats simply buying and holding the same ETF.
  • “Survives deflation” / luck-check = the result still looks real after correcting for how many strategies we tried (a guard against luck/overfitting). Beat buy & hold counts ETFs whose best strategy clears the ETF by a traded margin; the luck-check tally is the subset of those that also survive this correction.
  • Recipe / cell = the exact pipeline that produced a result: asset · bar-clock · labeling-method · sizing · threshold.
  • Bar-clock = strategies sample the market on event bars (e.g. equal dollar traded), not fixed clock time — so each bar carries comparable information.
  • Entry 0.40 = the model only takes a position when its conviction exceeds 0.40.

Calmar = annual return ÷ worst drawdown (higher is better) · vs. buy & hold = Calmar minus simply holding the ETF; bar length is relative to the largest edge on the board · Calmar history = best Calmar across successive rounds (line green if the latest is at/above the first tested, red if below) · signal = learnable structure in the label (validation AUC): 0.50 = none, above 0.60 = real; blank = not applicable to this recipe · significance — “holds up” = the Calmar survives the deflated-Sharpe / multiple-testing correction; “likely luck” = it does not, so the apparent edge is probably selection bias; “not assessed” = too few trades to test. What each asset rewards

The hard-won lesson among the core names: fully-validated machine-learned edges are scarce. GLD (gold trend-following) and UUP (dollar regime) are the two that survive the selection-bias audit; two-sided timing edges (EEM/TLT/IWM) looked great on a short window but decayed as the out-of-sample window grew. The 311-ETF universe screen is now widening the hunt and has surfaced a cluster of commodity & leveraged-equity fits (IAU, GDX, USO, SSO…) — screen-strong, validating before they earn a book seat.

The research arc

How the project got here — from a failed start, to the rule that governs the core board, to the universe-wide screen now running.

I · The null

Single-asset long-only ML couldn't beat buy-and-hold across 6 rounds → reframed to a v2 per-ETF tournament.

6-round NULL → tournament
II · The unlock

Long-only can't beat a declining asset; shorting + a directional label + ③ mean-reversion features unlocked TLT.

TLT 0.31 → 1.52
III · The correction

A bar-threshold look-ahead (full-series stats incl. OOS) was inflating results; the leak fix re-validated the whole board.

XLE 2.26 → 0.64
IV · Convergence

One rule governs the board — time when the hold is weak, hold when the trend is strong (f_timing_when).

7/7 at leak-free ceilings
V · The widening

With the fixed-12 frontier saturated, the hunt widened to all 311 QC-confirmed ETFs — race each against buy-and-hold, keep only genuine fits. A cluster of commodity & leveraged-equity names surfaced, now under validation.

311-ETF screen

Top insights

The most important things learned, each with the evidence that backs it.

  1. 01Meta-labeling crosses Calmar>3
  2. 02Causal mean-reversion features unlock mean-reverting ETFsTLT ③
    Adding causal RSI + Bollinger-%b oscillators (③) took TLT from 0.31 → 1.52 Calmar. Control (same axis/labeler, no features) stays at −0.14, so the lift is the features, not leakage.
  3. 03Ensembling two comparable labelers lifts; one dominant signal dilutesIWM R59
    Averaging calibrated triple_barrier + BGM predictions lifted IWM 0.93 → 1.14, but dilutes TLT (one signal already dominates). Ensemble only when two legs are individually strong.
  4. 04No-lookahead invariant: never filter trading bars by a future labelG3 audits
    Two enforced rules: (1) test/val predictions cover EVERY causal bar — a future label may filter only the FIT set, never which OOS bars trade; (2) bar thresholds fit on TRAIN minutes, not the full series (a magnitude-axis full-series threshold leaked OOS into bar placement — found + fixed).
  5. 05Selectivity beats exposure when directional accuracy is thinIWM R59
    On IWM's ensemble a tighter entry threshold (0.45) beat a looser one (0.40, no vol-throttle): +1.14 vs +0.94. Trade less, trade better.

How each outcome caused the next hypothesis. Drag · hover · double-click a phase cluster to expand. Full page: causal_graph.html
